Objection: Conceptual Opposition of Beginning and End
Al-Jurjani addresses an objection about conceptual opposition of beginning and end and clarifies the role of necessary and separable accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the concepts of beginning and end are opposites and how the commentator responds by distinguishing conceptual opposition from real opposition and emphasizing the role of necessary accidents.

Core Idea
Conceptual opposition of 'beginning' and 'end' does not entail real opposition of concrete points.

In this lesson, we address a subtle objection raised against the previous claim: if the concepts of 'beginning' and 'end' themselves are opposites (as al-Jurjani notes), then wouldn't any two points that serve as start and end be conceptually opposite, thus making movements contradictory? The commentator clarifies that the opposition in the second case (no difference) is only due to a necessary accident, and that even a separable accident can cause opposition if it is not delayed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with the objection
Identify the objection: 'if you say: between the concepts of beginning and end there is the opposition of contradiction...'
This objection challenges the earlier conclusion.
2
Understand the commentator's response
The commentator points to the phrase 'nor by a necessary accident' to argue that opposition in the second case is due to a necessary accident. This implies that if there is no necessary accident, there is no opposition.
The response relies on the distinction between necessary and separable accidents.
3
Reflect on the further point about separable accidents
The commentator mentions that even a separable accident (if it is not delayed) can cause opposition. This means the accident need not be permanent; as long as it accompanies the point in a timely manner, it can still cause opposition of movements.
The author's statement about induction suggests that in practice, such accidents are found only as necessary.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Will you let go of the superficial opposition today?

4 min
Opposition of Ascending and Descending Motions
Argument that accidental endpoint opposition causes essential motion opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how accidental opposition of endpoints causes essential opposition in ascending and descending rectilinear motions.

Core Idea
Opposition in motions stems from accidental, not essential, differences in endpoints.

This passage from a classical work of theology and philosophy examines whether there is genuine opposition between ascending and descending straight-line motions. The author addresses a common misconception that opposition arises from the endpoints themselves, and clarifies that it is only through accidental attributes that such opposition emerges, leading to a deeper understanding of the nature of motion and its categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a statement of a view, then refines it.
2
Identify the initial claim
What is the view presented at the start? Mark the phrase 'لا تضاد في الحركة المستقيمة الصاعدة والهابطة' (there is no opposition in straight motion of ascending and descending).
3
Understand the distinction between essential and accidental
The passage distinguishes between opposition 'بالذات' (essentially) and 'بالعرض' (accidentally). Notice how endpoints are said to not differ essentially or in necessary accident.
This distinction is crucial for the argument.
4
Trace the causation chain
Follow how accidental opposition of endpoints (e.g., one start, one end in opposite directions) becomes a cause for essential opposition of the motions themselves.
The author says: 'صار تضادهما بالعرض سبباً لتضاد الصاعدة والهابطة بالذات' (their accidental opposition became a cause for the essential opposition of ascending and descending).
5
Apply to opposite directions
The passage concludes that the same logic applies to motions in opposite directions (e.g., left and right). Think of another example to test your understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال : لا تضاد في الحركة المستقيمة الصاعدة والهابطة فعليك بالتأمل ) وقد لا يختلفان أصلا أي لا يختلف مبدأ الحركة ومنتهاها لا بحسب الماهية ولا بحسب عارض لازم ) بل يتفق إن صار أحدهما مبدأ ) لحركة ) والآخر منتهى ( لها ، فإذا فرض حركة أخرى من هذا المنتهى إلى ذلك المبدأ لم تكن مضادة للأولى، إذ لا تضاد بين المبدأين ولا بين المنتهيين لا بالذات ولا بالعرض وصار تضادهما بالعرض سبباً لتضاد الصاعدة والهابطة بالذات، فإنهما معنيان وجوديان يمتنع اجتماعهما في موضوع واحد وبينهما غاية الخلاف، وكذا حال الحركتين الواقعتين في جهتين متقابلتين وقد يقال : لا تضاد في الحركة المستقيمة الصاعدة والهابطة فعليك بالتأمل ) وقد لا يختلفان أصلا أي لا يختلف مبدأ الحركة ومنتهاها لا بحسب الماهية ولا بحسب عارض لازم ) بل يتفق إن صار أحدهما مبدأ ) لحركة ) والآخر منتهى ( لها ، فإذا فرض حركة أخرى من هذا المنتهى إلى ذلك المبدأ لم تكن مضادة للأولى، إذ لا تضاد بين المبدأين ولا بين المنتهيين لا بالذات ولا بالعرض
It may be said: There is no opposition in the straight motion of ascending and descending, so reflect. And they [the starting point and ending point] do not differ at all, i.e., the starting point of the motion and its ending point do not differ either in essence or in a necessary accident. Rather they agree, if one becomes a starting point for a motion and the other an ending point for it, then if another motion is assumed from this ending point to that starting point, it would not be opposed to the first, since there is no opposition between the two starting points nor between the two ending points, either essentially or accidentally. And their accidental opposition became a cause for the essential opposition of ascending and descending, for they are two existential meanings that cannot coexist in one subject and between them is utmost difference. And likewise the case of two motions occurring in two opposite directions. And it may be said: There is no opposition in the straight motion of ascending and descending, so reflect. And they do not differ at all, i.e., the starting point of the motion and its ending point do not differ either in essence or in a necessary accident. Rather they agree, if one becomes a starting point for a motion and the other an ending point for it, then if another motion is assumed from this ending point to that starting point, it would not be opposed to the first, since there is no opposition between the two starting points nor between the two ending points, either essentially or accidentally.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage explains the basis of opposition between ascending and descending rectilinear motions. It begins by stating a view that there is no opposition in straight motion, then qualifies it: if the endpoints (starting and ending points) of the motion do not differ in essence or in a necessary accident, then indeed there is no opposition. However, if one endpoint is a starting point for one motion and the other endpoint is an ending point for another motion, and the endpoints are accidentally opposite (e.g., one is high and the other low in a relative sense), then the motions become essentially opposed. The passage emphasizes that the two motions are existential meanings that cannot coexist in one subject and have utmost difference. It also mentions that the same applies to motions in opposite directions (e.g., left-right). The commentary points out that accidental opposition of endpoints causes essential opposition in the motions, a point supported by reference to Avicenna's al-Shifa.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Opposition between ascending and descending motions is due to the essential opposition of their starting and ending points.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the endpoints themselves do not oppose essentially; rather, it is their accidental attributes that cause the motions to be essentially opposed.

Checkpoint
What causes the essential opposition between ascending and descending motions according to this passage?
A) The intrinsic opposition of their starting and ending points
B) The accidental opposition of their starting and ending points
C) The difference in speed
D) The difference in direction

Key Takeaway
Accidental opposition of endpoints is the underlying cause for the essential opposition between ascending and descending motions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage teaches that endpoints themselves do not differ in essence. When you judge a person or situation, do you focus on the accidental endpoints (e.g., outward differences) rather than the essential reality? Can you practice seeing the essential sameness beneath superficial opposition?
?
Ascending and descending cannot coexist in the same subject. Are there opposing desires within you that you treat as irreconcilable? How might the insight that the opposition arises from accidental attributes help you integrate them or choose one without inner conflict?

Opposite Motions in Opposite Directions
Explains opposition of motions in opposite directions and the first objection/answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why motions in opposite directions are considered opposite due to the opposition of their starting and ending points, and how this relates to the concepts of mabda' and muntaha.

Core Idea
Motions are opposite when their endpoints are opposite, whether essentially or accidentally.

This lesson examines a specific case: motions from right to left and left to right. While the directions themselves are not inherently opposed, the relationship between their starting and ending points makes them opposite. We will also encounter an objection: if the concepts of 'start' and 'end' are always opposite, then all motions would be opposite. The answer distinguishes between essential and accidental opposition of endpoints.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on right-left motion
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the author connects opposition of motions to opposition of starting and ending points.
2
Understand the objection
The objection states that since the concepts of start and end are opposite in themselves, any two distinct points would make motions opposite. Why isn't that the case?
3
Explore the answer from al-Shifa
The answer from al-Shifa explains that endpoints can be opposite in two ways: essentially (like black/white) or accidentally (like high/low due to nearness). Only when endpoints are essentially opposite or when their difference prevents continuous motion without return does opposition arise.
This distinguishes between straight and curved motions.

His saying: (And likewise the case of the two motions, etc.) like the motion occurring from right to left and vice versa, for they are two opposites, due to the opposition of their starting point and ending point, for the two directions, even if they are starting points, yet between them is utmost difference after consideration. So likewise the two motions that are opposite according to them have between them utmost difference such that one cannot become the other, unlike the motion from right to left, for they are intent of motion from left to right considering the change of right to left. His saying: (Between the concepts of starting point and ending point, etc.) He said in al-Shifa in explaining the motion from one end of an arc to another end of an arc, and the opposite, and the arc is one and the same: they are not opposite unless the starting point and ending point are opposites due to the starting-ness and ending-ness, but rather because they are starting point and ending point of motion, not in any way whatsoever, but because they are starting point and ending point of the motion in a way that the starting point is not the same as the ending point in its continuity, so that the starting point and ending point are valid from the aspect of measurement to that. That only happens when the starting point is not the ending point and the ending point is not the starting point, for that cannot come together. And if that is the case, you have known that the two on the arc are opposite. Between the ascending... His saying: (Not) according to a necessary accident suggests that opposition in the second division is only due to the difference of starting point and ending point according to a necessary accident. So on this, there is no opposition in straight motion except between ascending and descending. And his saying: I say: There is no doubt... suggests that the non-delay of the accident that is a cause for opposition of starting point and ending point suffices for the opposition of the motion even if it is separable, unless his words are based on the fact that this accident is found only as necessary by induction. [PAGE_251] The Fourth Observatory - The Eighth Purpose: Opposing Motions: Between Ascending and Descending. 251. Their essences have opposition according to the accident, so the two motions are opposite on the analogy of what passed in ascending and descending. I say: There is no doubt that the establishment of these two accidents for their essences is posterior to the existence of the motion, so the opposition of these two accidents cannot be a cause for the opposition of the two motions, unlike nearness and farness from his words: The one does not oppose the other because the motion, according to that saying, does not occur to it from the aspect of motion as curvilinear that its starting point is different from its ending point in essential difference, rather that occurs due to cutting across and pausing that happens. Were it not for that, continuous direction towards the very starting point would be valid, and it would be one continuous motion with no return. End quote. And it is known from that that the cause for the opposition of the two circular motions on one and the straight motions in one distance is that the obtaining of starting point and ending point in them is according to assumption and coincidence, unlike ascending and descending, for the difference of starting point in them is essential; it does not allow continuity in them of the starting point being the ending point nor the ending point being the starting point. His saying: (Posterior to...) It is after the existence of the motion that one extremity becomes its starting point and the other its ending point. His saying: So the opposition of these two accidents cannot be etc., because the posterior cannot be a cause of the prior. But the discussion is about the priority of the opposition over these two accidents, because motion is described as opposition only after its existence; it is at the moment of reaching the extremity, and that is the moment of being described as starting-ness and ending-ness. And this meaning is found in the New Commentary on al-Tajrid that the establishment of these two accidents for their essences is posterior to the existence of the two motions, and likewise their opposition, and there is no improbability in one of the two posterior attributes being a cause of the other. His saying: (Unlike nearness, etc.) This contradicts what is in al-Shifa that the opposing motions whose extremities are opposite are only conceivable in two ways: one is that their extremities are opposite by real opposition in their essences, like blackness and whiteness; and the second is that their extremities are not opposite in their essences and quiddities but due to an external thing. And this is conceivable in two aspects: one relative to the motion, and the second relative to things external to the motion, such as the two ends of the continuous distance between heaven and earth: they are two points or places, and the nature of the two points and places is not opposite nor does it oppose like the opposition of blackness and whiteness, but they oppose due to an external thing. That external thing is either not related to the relation to motion or is related to it. As for what is external to the relation to motion, it is that one of the two ends is at the utmost nearness and the second at the utmost farness, so it becomes an end; from that it follows that it was high, and the other it follows that it was low. As for what is related to the relation to motion, it is like when one of the two ends has an accident. His saying: I say: There is no doubt, etc.) It was objected to him: Just as the establishment of these two accidents for their essences is posterior to the existence of the two motions, so also their opposition is posterior to their existence, and there is no improbability in one of the two posterior attributes being a cause of the other. His answer: The establishment of the totality of the mentioned accidents is temporally posterior to the existence of the two motions, because the description of being an ending point for the ending point only occurs after the cessation of motion, although the description of being a starting point is established for the starting point before cessation. As for opposition, motions are described with it at the time of their existence by consideration of direction, as he indicated in the verification that the opposition of motions is not based on obtaining at the extremities. Thus the posteriority of opposition to motion is only essential, and the posterior cannot be understood as prior; so reflect.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage extends the analysis of opposing motions to motions in opposite directions (e.g., right to left and left to right). The commentator explains that these motions are opposite due to the opposition of their starting and ending points, even if the directions are not essentially opposite. The passage then addresses an objection: the very concepts of 'starting point' and 'ending point' are opposite by nature (as one is a beginning and the other an end), so why should they not cause opposition in all motions? The answer, drawn from al-Shifa, distinguishes between cases where the endpoints are essentially opposite (like black and white) and where they are accidentally opposite (like high and low due to nearness/farness). In curved motions (arcs), the endpoints are not necessarily opposite unless the starting point and ending point are different in a way that prevents continuous motion without return. The discussion then turns to a key objection: the accidental attributes of 'being a starting point' and 'being an ending point' are posterior to the existence of the motion, so how can they be the cause of opposition which seems to be simultaneous? The answer clarifies that the posteriority is temporal for the ending point description (it occurs after motion stops), but the starting point description is present from the beginning. The opposition, however, is described during the motion based on direction, not on the actual attainment of the endpoints. So the opposition is not caused by the posterior accidents but is an essential attribute of the motion itself, even if the cause is the accidental opposition of the endpoints. The passage ends by urging deep reflection.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All motions with different starting and ending points are opposite.
Correction: Only when the endpoints are essentially opposite or when their difference prevents continuous motion without return does opposition arise.

Key Takeaway
The opposition of motions in opposite directions is rooted in the opposition of their endpoints, which can be either essential or accidental.

The Timing Objection: Can Posterior Attributes Cause Opposition?
Addresses the timing objection and its resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the attributes of 'being a starting point' and 'being an ending point' are posterior to motion existence, and the resolution that opposition is described during motion based on direction, not on attainment.

Core Idea
Motion opposition is not caused by posterior attributes; it is inherent in the directional tendency.

A key objection arises: if motion opposition depends on the attributes of being a starting point or ending point, and these attributes only occur after the motion exists (or after it stops), how can they be the cause? The response clarifies that opposition is attributed to motions during their existence by consideration of direction (tawajjuh), not by the actual attainment of the endpoints. This lesson dissects that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The passage states that the two accidents (being a starting point and being an ending point) are posterior to the existence of motion, so they cannot cause opposition.
Note the phrase 'mutā'akhkhir' (posterior).
2
Understand the response
The response argues that the description of opposition occurs during motion based on direction, not after it reaches the endpoint. The starting point attribute is present from the beginning, so it is not entirely posterior.
Also, the ending point attribute appears after motion stops, but opposition is already present.
3
Reflect on the distinction
The discussion differentiates between temporal posteriority and essential posteriority. The opposition is not caused by the accidents but is simultaneous with the motion's direction.
The passage ends with 'fa-tadabbar' (so reflect), urging deep thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وكذا حال الحركتين إلخ كالحركة الواقعة من اليمين إلى اليسار وبالعكس فإنهما متضادان، لتضاد مبدئهما ومنتهاهما فإن الجهتين وإن كانت مبدأين لكنه بينهما غاية الخلاف بعد الاعتبار، فكذا الحركتان المتضادتان بحسبهما بينهما غاية الخلاف بحيث لا يمكن أن يصير إحداهما الأخرى بخلاف الحركة من اليمين إلى اليسار فإنهما قصد حركة من اليسار إلى اليمين باعتبار تبدل اليمين إلى اليسار. قوله : ( بين مفهومي المبدأ والمنتهى إلخ قال في الشفاء في بيان الحركة التي من طرف قوس إلى طرف قوس آخر ، والتي بالعكس والقوس واحد بعينها لا تكون متضادة إن لم يكن المبدأ والمنتهى ضدين لأجل المبدئية والمنتهية، بل لأجل أنهما مبدأ ومنتهى حركة ولا كيف ما اتفق لأجل أنهما مبدأ ومنتهى الحركة بصفة لا تكون مبدأهما هو بعينه منها في استمرارها حتى يصح المبدأ والمنتهى من جهة القياس إلى ذلك، إنما يتفق حيث يكون المبدأ منتهى ولا المنتهى مبدأ فذلك هو الذي لا يجتمع وإذا كان كذلك فقد عرفت أن اللتين على القوس التعاند بين الصاعدة قوله : (ولا) بحسب عارض (لازم يشعر بأن التضاد في القسم الثاني إنما هو بسبب اختلاف المبدأ والمنتهى بحسب عارض لازم فعلى هذا لاتضاد في الحركة المستقيمة إلا بين والهابطة، وقوله : قلت : لا شك إلخ يشعر بأن عدم تأخر العارض الذي يكون سبباً لتضاد المبدأ والمنتهى يكفي في تضاد الحركة ولو كان مفارقاً، اللهم إلا أن يبنى كلامه على أن هذا العارض ما وجد إلا لازما بالاستقراء .  المرصد الرابع - المقصد الثامن : الحركات المتضادة : بين الصاعدة والهابطة ٢٥١ ذاتيهما تضاد بحسب العارض فتكون الحركتان متضادتين على قياس ما مر في الصاعدة والهابطة قلت : لا شك أن ثبوت هذين العارضين لذاتيهما متأخر عن وجود . الحركة، فلا يكون تضاد هذين العارضين علة لتضاد الحركتين بخلاف القرب والبعد من كلامه الواحدة لا تتضادان لأن الحركة على تلك القول لا يعرض لها من حيث الحركة قوسية أن يكون مبدؤها غير منتهاها مغايرة ذاتية، بل يعرض لذلك لقطع العرض ووقوف يتفق، ولولا ذلك لصح التوجه المستمر إلى المبدأ بعينه وهي حركة واحدة متصلة لا رجوع فيها انتهى . ويعلم من أن الموجب لتضاد الحركتين المستديرتين على واحد والمستقيمتين في مسافة واحدة فإن حصول المبدأ والمنتهى فيهما بحسب الفرض والاتفاق بخلاف الصاعدة والهابطة فإن تغاير المبدأ فيها ذاتية لا يجعل الاستمرار فيهما المبدأ منتهى ولا المنتهى مبدأ . قوله : ( متأخر عن إلخ ) فإنه بعد وجود الحركة يصير طرف مبدأ لها والآخر منتهى له . قوله : فلا يكون تضاد هذين العارضين إلى آخره لأن المتأخر لا يكون علة للمتقدم ولكن الكلام في تقدم التضاد على هذين العارضين لأن الحركة إنما توصف بالتضاد بعد وجودها، إنما هو حال الوصول إلى الطرف، وهو حال الاتصاف بالمبدئية والمنتهية، وهذا المعنى ما في الشرح الجديد للتجريد من أن ثبوت هذين العارضين لذاتيهما متأخر عن وجود الحركتين، فكذا تضادهما ولا استبعاد في أن يكون أحد الوصفين المتأخرين علة للآخر. قوله : (بخلاف القرب إلخ هذا مخالف لما في الشفاء من أن الحركات المتضادة التي ) تقابل أطرافها، وإنما يتصور على وجهين أحدهما : أن يكون أطرافها يتقابل بالتضاد الحقيقي في ذواتها مثل السواد والبياض والثاني : أن لا يتقابل أطرافها في ذواتها وماهياتها بل لأمر خارج، وهذا يتصور من جهتين إحداهما بالقياس إلى الحركة والثانية بالقياس إلى أمور خارجة عن الحركة، مثل أن طرفي المسافة المتصلة بين السماء والأرض هما نقطتان أو مكانان وطباع النقطتين والمكانين لا يتضاد ولا يتقابل تقابل السواد والبياض، بل يتقابل لأمر خارج وذلك الأمر إما غير متعلق النسبة إلى الحركة وإما متعلق بها، أما الخارج عن النسبة إلى الحركة فبأن يكون أحد الطرفين في غاية القرب والطرف الثاني في غاية البعد، فيكون طرفاً منه لزمه أن كان علواً وآخر لزمه إن كان سفلاً. وأما المتعلق بالنسبة إلى الحركة فمثل أن يكون أحد الطرفين عرض له قوله : قلت : لا شك إلخ) قيل عليه كما أن ثبوت هذين العارضين لذاتيهما متأخر عن وجود الحركتين، فكذا تضادهما أيضاً متأخر عن وجودهما، ولا استبعاد في أن يكون أحد الوصفين المتأخرين علة للآخر، وجوابه أن ثبوت مجموع العارضين المذكورين متأخر عن وجود الحركتين زماناً، لأن وصف المنتهائية للمنتهى إنما يعرض بعد انقطاع الحركة، وإن كان وصف المبدئية ثبت للمبدأ قبل الانقطاع، وأما التضاد فيوصف به الحركات حال وجودها باعتبار التوجه كما أشار إليه في تحقيق أن ليس تضاد الحركات باعتبار الحصول في الأطراف، فتأخر التضاد عن الحركة ليس إلا بالذات ولا يعقل عليه المتأخر للمتقدم فتأمل.
His saying: (And likewise the case of the two motions, etc.) like the motion occurring from right to left and vice versa, for they are two opposites, due to the opposition of their starting point and ending point, for the two directions, even if they are starting points, yet between them is utmost difference after consideration. So likewise the two motions that are opposite according to them have between them utmost difference such that one cannot become the other, unlike the motion from right to left, for they are intent of motion from left to right considering the change of right to left. His saying: (Between the concepts of starting point and ending point, etc.) He said in al-Shifa in explaining the motion from one end of an arc to another end of an arc, and the opposite, and the arc is one and the same: they are not opposite unless the starting point and ending point are opposites due to the starting-ness and ending-ness, but rather because they are starting point and ending point of motion, not in any way whatsoever, but because they are starting point and ending point of the motion in a way that the starting point is not the same as the ending point in its continuity, so that the starting point and ending point are valid from the aspect of measurement to that. That only happens when the starting point is not the ending point and the ending point is not the starting point, for that cannot come together. And if that is the case, you have known that the two on the arc are opposite. Between the ascending... His saying: (Not) according to a necessary accident suggests that opposition in the second division is only due to the difference of starting point and ending point according to a necessary accident. So on this, there is no opposition in straight motion except between ascending and descending. And his saying: I say: There is no doubt... suggests that the non-delay of the accident that is a cause for opposition of starting point and ending point suffices for the opposition of the motion even if it is separable, unless his words are based on the fact that this accident is found only as necessary by induction. [PAGE_251] The Fourth Observatory - The Eighth Purpose: Opposing Motions: Between Ascending and Descending. 251. Their essences have opposition according to the accident, so the two motions are opposite on the analogy of what passed in ascending and descending. I say: There is no doubt that the establishment of these two accidents for their essences is posterior to the existence of the motion, so the opposition of these two accidents cannot be a cause for the opposition of the two motions, unlike nearness and farness from his words: The one does not oppose the other because the motion, according to that saying, does not occur to it from the aspect of motion as curvilinear that its starting point is different from its ending point in essential difference, rather that occurs due to cutting across and pausing that happens. Were it not for that, continuous direction towards the very starting point would be valid, and it would be one continuous motion with no return. End quote. And it is known from that that the cause for the opposition of the two circular motions on one and the straight motions in one distance is that the obtaining of starting point and ending point in them is according to assumption and coincidence, unlike ascending and descending, for the difference of starting point in them is essential; it does not allow continuity in them of the starting point being the ending point nor the ending point being the starting point. His saying: (Posterior to...) It is after the existence of the motion that one extremity becomes its starting point and the other its ending point. His saying: So the opposition of these two accidents cannot be etc., because the posterior cannot be a cause of the prior. But the discussion is about the priority of the opposition over these two accidents, because motion is described as opposition only after its existence; it is at the moment of reaching the extremity, and that is the moment of being described as starting-ness and ending-ness. And this meaning is found in the New Commentary on al-Tajrid that the establishment of these two accidents for their essences is posterior to the existence of the two motions, and likewise their opposition, and there is no improbability in one of the two posterior attributes being a cause of the other. His saying: (Unlike nearness, etc.) This contradicts what is in al-Shifa that the opposing motions whose extremities are opposite are only conceivable in two ways: one is that their extremities are opposite by real opposition in their essences, like blackness and whiteness; and the second is that their extremities are not opposite in their essences and quiddities but due to an external thing. And this is conceivable in two aspects: one relative to the motion, and the second relative to things external to the motion, such as the two ends of the continuous distance between heaven and earth: they are two points or places, and the nature of the two points and places is not opposite nor does it oppose like the opposition of blackness and whiteness, but they oppose due to an external thing. That external thing is either not related to the relation to motion or is related to it. As for what is external to the relation to motion, it is that one of the two ends is at the utmost nearness and the second at the utmost farness, so it becomes an end; from that it follows that it was high, and the other it follows that it was low. As for what is related to the relation to motion, it is like when one of the two ends has an accident. His saying: I say: There is no doubt, etc.) It was objected to him: Just as the establishment of these two accidents for their essences is posterior to the existence of the two motions, so also their opposition is posterior to their existence, and there is no improbability in one of the two posterior attributes being a cause of the other. His answer: The establishment of the totality of the mentioned accidents is temporally posterior to the existence of the two motions, because the description of being an ending point for the ending point only occurs after the cessation of motion, although the description of being a starting point is established for the starting point before cessation. As for opposition, motions are described with it at the time of their existence by consideration of direction, as he indicated in the verification that the opposition of motions is not based on obtaining at the extremities. Thus the posteriority of opposition to motion is only essential, and the posterior cannot be understood as prior; so reflect.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage extends the analysis of opposing motions to motions in opposite directions (e.g., right to left and left to right). The commentator explains that these motions are opposite due to the opposition of their starting and ending points, even if the directions are not essentially opposite. The passage then addresses an objection: the very concepts of 'starting point' and 'ending point' are opposite by nature (as one is a beginning and the other an end), so why should they not cause opposition in all motions? The answer, drawn from al-Shifa, distinguishes between cases where the endpoints are essentially opposite (like black and white) and where they are accidentally opposite (like high and low due to nearness/farness). In curved motions (arcs), the endpoints are not necessarily opposite unless the starting point and ending point are different in a way that prevents continuous motion without return. The discussion then turns to a key objection: the accidental attributes of 'being a starting point' and 'being an ending point' are posterior to the existence of the motion, so how can they be the cause of opposition which seems to be simultaneous? The answer clarifies that the posteriority is temporal for the ending point description (it occurs after motion stops), but the starting point description is present from the beginning. The opposition, however, is described during the motion based on direction, not on the actual attainment of the endpoints. So the opposition is not caused by the posterior accidents but is an essential attribute of the motion itself, even if the cause is the accidental opposition of the endpoints. The passage ends by urging deep reflection.

Key Terms
عارض لازم
متأخر
التوجه
التضاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion opposition is caused by the endpoints being opposite after the motion stops.
Correction: Opposition is attributed during motion based on directional tendency, not on post-motion attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the final response, why does the temporal posteriority of the ending point description not prevent it from being involved in motion opposition?
A) Because opposition is also temporally posterior
B) Because opposition is described during motion based on direction, not on attaining the endpoint
C) Because the starting point description is also temporally posterior
D) Because the cause must always be prior

Key Takeaway
The opposition of motions is not caused by later-acquired attributes; it is inherent in the motion's direction from its start.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are moving toward a clear goal, do you tend to define yourself by where you started (your past) or by where you are heading (your future)? Which of these actually shapes your present direction and opposition to sin?
?
In your own journey of faith, do you delay judging your actions until you reach an endpoint (like death or a major milestone), or do you examine the direction of your heart while you are still moving? Why does that distinction matter urgently for your repentance?
?
If your ultimate purpose is to meet Allah, your ending point attribute is 'being a slave who has reached the Hereafter.' But that attribute is temporally posterior. Right now, what is the direction (tawajjuh) of your life's motion? Are you actually loving what is opposite to that end?

Objection and Refutation on Opposition of Motions
Al-Jurjani objects that accidental properties cannot cause motion opposition and responds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Jurjani defends the possibility of accidental properties causing motion opposition despite their temporal posteriority.

Core Idea
Posteriority does not prevent causality when both cause and effect are posterior.

In this passage, Al-Jurjani responds to an objection that accidental properties like 'being a start' or 'being an end' cannot cause opposition because they arise only after the motion exists. He argues that this objection misses the point: the opposition itself is also posterior, so one posterior description can indeed cause another. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Notice how the objector claims that accidental properties are posterior to motion. The key phrase is 'لا شك أن ثبوت هذين العارضين... متأخر عن وجود الحركة'.
2
Understand why posteriority blocks causality
The objector argues that if X is posterior to Y, X cannot be the cause of Y because cause must precede effect.
3
Examine Al-Jurjani's response
He points out that the opposition of motions is also posterior—it happens when motion reaches an endpoint. So both descriptions are posterior, and one can cause the other.
4
Connect to the broader principle
This shows that in kalam, causal relations can involve simultaneous or co-posterior events, not just temporal priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذاتيهما تضاد بحسب العارض فَتَكون الحركتان متضادتين على قياس ما مر في الصاعدة والهابطة قلت : لا شك أن ثبوت هذين العارضين لذاتيهما متأخر عن وجود . الحركة، فلا يكون تضاد هذين العارضين علة لتضاد الحركتين بخلاف القرب والبعد من كلامه قوله : ( متأخر عن إلخ ) فإنه بعد وجود الحركة يصير طرف مبدأ لها والآخر منتهى له . قوله : فلا يكون تضاد هذين العارضين إلى آخره لأن المتأخر لا يكون علة للمتقدم ولكن الكلام في تقدم التضاد على هذين العارضين لأن الحركة إنما توصف بالتضاد بعد وجودها، إنما هو حال الوصول إلى الطرف، وهو حال الاتصاف بالمبدئية والمنتهية، وهذا المعنى ما في الشرح الجديد للتجريد من أن ثبوت هذين العارضين لذاتيهما متأخر عن وجود الحركتين، فكذا تضادهما ولا استبعاد في أن يكون أحد الوصفين المتأخرين علة للآخر.
Their essences have opposition according to the accidental property, so the two motions become opposed on the pattern of what passed in ascending and descending. I said: There is no doubt that the establishment of these two accidental properties to their essences is posterior to the existence of motion, so the opposition of these two accidental properties is not a cause for the opposition of the two motions, contrary to proximity and distance. His statement: (posterior to etc.) for after the existence of motion, one side becomes its start and the other its end. His statement: so the opposition of these two accidental properties etc. because the posterior is not a cause for the prior, but the discussion is about the priority of opposition over these two accidental properties, because motion is only described by opposition after its existence, and that is only at the moment of reaching the side, which is the moment of being described by start-ness and end-ness. This meaning is what is in the New Commentary on al-Tajrid, that the establishment of these two accidental properties to their essences is posterior to the existence of the two motions, and likewise their opposition, and there is no improbability in one of the two posterior descriptions being a cause for the other.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer concerning the basis of opposition between ascending and descending motions. The objector argues that if opposition is said to arise from accidental properties (being a start or an end), those properties are posterior to the motion itself, so they cannot be the cause of opposition. The answer clarifies that while the accidental properties are indeed posterior, the opposition of the motions is also posterior, being simultaneous with the attainment of the endpoint; therefore one posterior thing can be a cause of another posterior thing, as explained in the New Commentary on al-Tajrid.

Key Terms

عارض
مبدأ
منتهى
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that temporal posteriority always prevents a thing from being a cause.
Correction: The text shows that essential posteriority (not temporal) allows causality when both cause and effect are posterior.

Checkpoint
According to the response, why can the opposition of accidental properties be a cause for the opposition of motions?
A) Because the accidental properties are prior to the motion.
B) Because the opposition is also posterior, and one posterior thing can cause another.
C) Because the motion itself causes the accidental properties.
D) Because the opposition is intrinsic to the essences.

Key Takeaway
The opposition of motions can be caused by accidental properties that are themselves posterior, since the opposition is also posterior.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you assume that because something happened 'too late' it cannot change anything, reflect on this lesson: posterior things can be causes. What change have you been postponing that you now realize can still be effective? Commit to one specific action today.
?
The objector insisted on temporal priority for causality. In your own life, where do you demand that change must come before you act? Where can you reverse that order and act first, letting the change follow?
?
This lesson shows that even describing a motion after its existence gives it meaning. What past action or failure do you need to re-describe now in light of new understanding? How will that re-description lead you to repent and move forward?

Distinguishing Temporal from Essential Posteriority
Al-Jurjani answers a further objection by distinguishing temporal from essential posteriority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why temporal posteriority prevents causation but essential posteriority does not, in the context of motions and their accidental properties.

Core Idea
Not all 'after' is the same: temporal sequence blocks backward causation, but logical dependence does not.

We now encounter a subtle objection that could overturn the entire argument about motion and opposition. The objector argues that if the accidental properties come after the motions, why couldn't the opposition (also after) cause them? Al-Jurjani's answer hinges on a crucial distinction between two kinds of posteriority—one measured by time, the other by logical priority. Mastering this distinction is essential for following later arguments about causation and precedence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: it says both the attributes and the opposition are posterior to motion, so why can't one posterior cause the other?
The objector is trying to use the same reasoning against the author.
2
Grasp the distinction
Notice how the answer separates temporal posteriority (the attributes occur after motion stops) from essential posteriority (opposition is described during motion, but logically depends on motion).
Temporal: measured by time. Essential: measured by logical dependence.
3
Apply the distinction
Understand why only temporal posteriority would make causation from a later to an earlier impossible. Essential posteriority allows causation because the cause exists simultaneously with the effect.
This distinction recurs in many kalām arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : قلت : لا شك إلخ) قيل عليه كما أن ثبوت هذين العارضين لذاتيهما متأخر عن وجود الحركتين، فكذا تضادهما أيضاً متأخر عن وجودهما، ولا استبعاد في أن يكون أحد الوصفين المتأخرين علة للآخر، وجوابه أن ثبوت مجموع العارضين المذكورين متأخر عن وجود الحركتين زماناً، لأن وصف المنتهائية للمنتهى إنما يعرض بعد انقطاع الحركة، وإن كان وصف المبدئية ثبت للمبدأ قبل الانقطاع، وأما التضاد فيوصف به الحركات حال وجودها باعتبار التوجه كما أشار إليه في تحقيق أن ليس تضاد الحركات باعتبار الحصول في الأطراف، فتأخر التضاد عن الحركة ليس إلا بالذات ولا يعقل عليه المتأخر للمتقدم فتأمل.
His statement: 'I said: There is no doubt etc.' It was objected: just as the establishment of these two accidental properties to their essences is posterior to the existence of the two motions, so too is their opposition also posterior to their existence, and there is no improbability in one of the two posterior descriptions being a cause for the other. Its answer: The establishment of the totality of the mentioned accidental properties is temporally posterior to the existence of the two motions, because the description of being an end for the endpoint only occurs after the cessation of motion, although the description of being a start is established for the start before cessation. As for opposition, the motions are described by it while they exist, by virtue of direction, as he indicated in the investigation that the opposition of motions is not by virtue of occurring at the endpoints. Thus the posteriority of opposition to motion is only essential, and it is inconceivable that the posterior be prior to the prior. Contemplate.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents a further objection and its detailed answer. The objector says: even if the accidental properties are posterior, the opposition is also posterior, so why can't the opposition be the cause? The answer distinguishes temporal posteriority from essential posteriority: the accidental properties (like being an end) are temporally posterior, occurring only after motion stops, while opposition characterizes the motions while they are ongoing, by virtue of their direction. Thus the opposition is only essentially posterior (i.e., logically dependent on motion), and this does not prevent it from being a cause of the temporally posterior properties.

Key Terms
زماناً
بالذات
توجه
انقطاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might conflate temporal posteriority with essential posteriority, thinking that any kind of posteriority prevents causation.
Correction: The text clarifies that only temporal posteriority prevents causation from a prior to a posterior; essential posteriority does not.

Checkpoint
Why does the answer say the accidental properties are temporally posterior while the opposition is only essentially posterior?
A) Because opposition exists before motion.
B) Because the accidental properties occur after motion ceases, but opposition is described during motion.
C) Because both are equally posterior in time.
D) Because opposition is not a real description.

Key Takeaway
The crucial distinction between temporal and essential posteriority shows that only temporal sequence prevents a later cause, while logical dependence does not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mistaken a logical dependency for a temporal one, causing you to doubt that something could be a cause? In your struggle against a recurring sin, do you assume that because the sin came first, your repentance cannot erase its effects? This lesson shows that logical dependence can overturn that assumption—will you let that reshape your hope in Allah’s forgiveness?
?
The objection in the passage seems plausible: if two things are both later, one can cause the other. But the answer shows a hidden assumption. Where in your life are you making similar plausible assumptions about cause and effect that you have never examined? Will you dare to look deeper, even if it unsettles your worldview?
?
The text says 'it is inconceivable that the temporally posterior be prior to the temporally prior.' Do you live as if your past failures are temporally posterior to your future? They are not: they are past. But your beliefs about them may be essentially posterior—dependent on your present understanding. Will you let that essential dependence free you from being defined by what came before?

Actual vs Hypothetical Endpoints in Rectilinear and Circular Motions
Classification of actual vs hypothetical endpoints in motion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how start and end are attributed to rectilinear motion (actually) versus circular motion (hypothetically).

Core Idea
Rectilinear motion has actual endpoints; circular motion has only hypothetical ones.

This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif introduces a key distinction: while rectilinear motion has clearly defined start and end points, circular motion is continuous and its endpoints are merely assigned by hypothesis. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the distinction.
Notice the terms 'bi'l-fi'l' and 'bi'l-fard'.
2
Identify the two types of motion
The passage contrasts rectilinear motion (actual start/end) with circular motion (hypothetical start/end). Pause to see how each is described.
3
Understand why circular motion lacks actual endpoints
Reflect on the reasoning: since any point can serve as both start and end, there is no intrinsic differentiation. An actual point is not required; potentiality suffices.
This connects to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك أي اتصاف أحدهما بكونه مبدأ والآخر بكونه منتهى (قد يكون بالفعل كما في الحركة المستقيمة) فإن لها مبدأ متصفاً بالمبدائية بالفعل ولها كذلك (و) قد يكون ذلك الاتصاف ) بمجرد الفرض كما في الحركة المستديرة فإن أي جزء فرضت على الجسم المتحرك بالاستدارة كالفلك ( مبدأ للدور ومنتهى له باعتبارين) إذ الحركة عن كل جزء هي بعينها الحركة إلى ذلك الجزء فلا مبدأ ولا منتهى للمستديرة إلا بمجرد الفرض ( ولا تمايز فيه ) أي في الدائر حتى يثبت للدور ابتداء وانتهاء بالفعل (إلا) بما يعرض من موازاة أو فرض أو غير ذلك) من الشروق والغروب، وليس شيء منها موجبا للتمايز الخارجي، وليس من شرط وجود الحركة المستديرة أن يوجد هناك نقطة بالفعل لتكون مبدأ من وجه ومنتهى من وجه وإلا امتنع حركة الفلك بالاستدارة إذ لا وجود للنقطة بالفعل إلا بسبب القطع وهو عليه محال عندهم، بل يكفي لتحقق المستديرة كون النقطة بالقوة القريبة وهاهنا بحث وهو أن الحركة المستديرة حركة وضعية فيكون مبدؤها وكذا منتهاها وضعاً مخصوصاً، كما أن مبدأ الحركة الكيفية ومنتهاها كيف مخصوص فإذا فرض أن جسماً كان ساكناً ثم تحرك على نفسه، فالوضع الذي ابتدأت الحركة منه كان مبدأ لها، وإذا فرض سكونها ثانياً كان الوضع الذي انقطعت الحركة عنده منتهي لها سواء كان مماثلا للوضع الأول أو مخالفا له فقد ثبت للمستديرة مبدأ ومنتهى بالفعل كالمستقيمة نعم إذا فرض أن المستديرة أزلية أبدية كما هو مذهبهم في الحركات الفلكية لم يكن هناك مبدأ ولا منتهى بالفعل كما نبهناك عليه فيما سلف ولا يمكن مثل هذا الفرض في المستقيمة لتناهي الأبعاد وانقطاع الحركة بالرجوع والانعطاف فلا بد لها دائماً من مبدأ ومنتهى بالفعل، نعم إذا فرض أن جسماً تحرك على محيط دائرة حتى تمم دورة كان مبدؤها ومنتهاها واحداً بالذات مختلفاً بالاعتبار، إلا أن هذه حركة أينية في الاصطلاح مستديرة بحسب اللغة ( تنبيه . المبدأ مبدأ الحركة الواحدة والآخر عرض له منتهى فإنه صريح في أن تضاد الصاعدة والهابطة باعتبار كون ما منه وما إليه فيهما مضاداً ومخالفاً للآخر في المبدئية والمنتهية لا باعتبار أنه في غاية القرب أو في غاية البعد فإنه لا تعلق لهذين الاعتبارين بالحركة فضلاً عن أن يكون موجباً للتضاد . قوله : ( وهاهنا بحث إلخ ) مقصوداً لقائل إذا فرض ابتداء المستدبرة من نقطة كما يفرضون الدور بعينه كان المبدأ والمنتهى بمجرد الفرض لا أن الحركة الوضعية مبدؤها ومنتهاها النقطة حتى يرد ما ذكره الشارح .
And that, i.e., the description of one of them as being a start and the other as being an end, may be actual as in rectilinear motion, for it has a start actually described as start-ness and likewise an end. And that description may be merely hypothetical as in circular motion, for any part you hypothesize on a body moving circularly like the celestial sphere is a start for the cycle and an end for it under two aspects, since the motion from each part is identical to the motion to that part. So there is no start or end for circular motion except by hypothesis. And there is no differentiation in it, i.e., in the circle, such that a beginning and end are established for the cycle actually, except by something incidental like alignment or hypothesis or other things like sunrise and sunset, none of which necessitate external differentiation. And it is not a condition for the existence of circular motion that there exist an actual point to be a start in one respect and an end in another, otherwise the motion of the celestial sphere would be impossible, since an actual point exists only due to cutting, which is impossible for them. Rather, for the realization of circular motion, it suffices that the point be in proximate potentiality. And here is a discussion: Circular motion is a positional motion, so its start and likewise its end are a specific position. Just as the start of qualitative motion and its end are a specific quality. So if it is hypothesized that a body was stationary and then moved on itself, the position from which the motion began is its start, and if its rest is hypothesized secondly, the position at which motion ceases is its end, whether it is similar to the first position or different. Thus a start and end are established for circular motion actually like rectilinear. Yes, if circular motion is hypothesized as eternal and perpetual, as is their doctrine in celestial motions, then there is no actual start or end, as we cautioned earlier, and such a hypothesis is impossible in rectilinear motion due to the finitude of dimensions and the interruption of motion by return and turning, so it must always have an actual start and end. Yes, if it is hypothesized that a body moves on the circumference of a circle until completing a rotation, its start and end are identical in essence, different by consideration, except that this is a locative motion in terminology, circular in language. (Notice: The start – the start of a single motion and the other had an end occur to it – it is explicit that the opposition of ascending and descending is by virtue of that from which and to which in them being opposed and different from the other in start-ness and end-ness, not by virtue of being in extreme proximity or extreme distance, for these two considerations have no relation to motion, much less being a cause for opposition. His statement: (and here is a discussion etc.) is intended for someone who says: if the beginning of the circular motion is hypothesized from a point, as they hypothesize the cycle itself, the start and end are merely hypothetical, not that the positional motion has its start and end as the point, so that what the commentator mentioned would be refuted.)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage explains how start and end (mabda' and muntaha) are attributed to motions, distinguishing rectilinear from circular. Rectilinear motion has actual endpoints. Circular motion, being continuous and lack ing intrinsic differentiation, has only hypothetical endpoints unless something external (like alignment or a hypothesized point) provides a distinction. However, there is a discussion: if circular motion is considered as a positional motion (e.g., a body rotating on its axis), it can have actual starts and ends in terms of positions, similar to rectilinear motion, unless the motion is eternal (as in celestial spheres). The note (tanbih) emphasizes that the opposition of ascending and descending motions is based precisely on their intrinsic directions (from and to), not on accidental properties like extreme proximity or distance, which have no connection to motion itself.

Key Terms
مبدؤها
منتهاها
بالفعل
بالفرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, rectilinear motion has its start and end __________.
A) actually
B) hypothetically
C) both
D) neither

Key Takeaway
Rectilinear motion has actual endpoints; circular motion has only hypothetical ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that circular motion only requires potential endpoints, not actual ones. In your daily worship, do you wait for the 'perfect' actual moment to begin, or do you act on potential? What would change if you treated each moment as both a start and an end?
?
The passage stresses that circular motion has no actual differentiation—every point is both beginning and end. Does your spiritual journey feel this way—a continuous cycle where each act is both a fresh start and the culmination of what came before? How would that reframe your view of repentance and renewal?
?
If the celestial spheres move without an actual starting point, relying only on potential, what does that say about your own reliance on Allah's ongoing creation? Are you living as if you need a clear 'start' to change, or can you embrace the potential already within you to move toward Him right now?

The Positional Nature of Circular Motion: Actual Endpoints in Finite Cases
Discussion of circular motion as positional and its actual endpoints in finite cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that circular motion, as a positional motion, can have actual start and end points based on position, and how eternal motion differs.

Core Idea
Circular motion can have actual endpoints based on position, but eternal motion lacks them.

Having established that circular motion typically has only hypothetical endpoints, the text now considers a deeper discussion: if circular motion is considered as a positional change (haraka wad'iyya), it can actually have a start and end in terms of position, just like qualitative motion. However, for eternal motions like those of the celestial spheres, there is no actual start or end.

Guided Path
1
Read the discussion section
Read the passage starting with 'And here is a discussion' and its translation. This is a separate argument within the larger text.
2
Understand the concept of positional motion
Recognize that circular motion is a change in position (wad'), so its start and end are specific positions, similar to how qualitative motion has specific qualities as start and end.
3
Contrast finite rotation with eternal motion
Notice that for a finite rotation, the starting and ending positions are actual. But if the motion is eternal (as with celestial spheres), there is no actual start or end because the motion never began or ceased.

The Basis of Opposition in Ascending and Descending Motions
Clarification of the basis of opposition of ascending and descending motions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the opposition of ascending and descending motions is based on their intrinsic directions (from and to), not on accidental properties like extreme distance.

Core Idea
Motion opposition is due to the start and end being intrinsically opposed, not due to distance.

The passage concludes with a crucial clarification: when we say ascending and descending motions are opposed, it is because their 'from' and 'to' points are opposed in terms of being a start versus an end, not because one is near and the other far. This refines our understanding of motion opposition.

Guided Path
1
Read the tanbih (notice)
Read the final part of the passage, which begins with 'Notice:'. This is a clarifying remark.
2
Identify the mistaken view
The text rejects the idea that opposition is due to extreme proximity or distance. Note why these are irrelevant to motion itself.
3
Understand the correct basis
The correct basis is that ascending and descending have opposite 'from' and 'to' points: in ascent, the start is low and the end is high; in descent, it's reversed. This intrinsic direction is what causes opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So if it is hypothesized that a body was stationary and then moved on itself, the position from which the motion began is its start, and if its rest is hypothesized secondly, the position at which motion ceases is its end, whether it is similar to the first position or different. Thus a start and end are established for circular motion actually like rectilinear. Yes, if circular motion is hypothesized as eternal and perpetual, as is their doctrine in celestial motions, then there is no actual start or end, as we cautioned earlier, and such a hypothesis is impossible in rectilinear motion due to the finitude of dimensions and the interruption of motion by return and turning, so it must always have an actual start and end. Yes, if it is hypothesized that a body moves on the circumference of a circle until completing a rotation, its start and end are identical in essence, different by consideration, except that this is a locative motion in terminology, circular in language. (Notice: The start – the start of a single motion and the other had an end occur to it – it is explicit that the opposition of ascending and descending is by virtue of that from which and to which in them being opposed and different from the other in start-ness and end-ness, not by virtue of being in extreme proximity or extreme distance, for these two considerations have no relation to motion, much less being a cause for opposition. His statement: (and here is a discussion etc.) is intended for someone who says: if the beginning of the circular motion is hypothesized from a point, as they hypothesize the cycle itself, the start and end are merely hypothetical, not that the positional motion has its start and end as the point, so that what the commentator mentioned would be refuted.)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage explains how start and end (mabda' and muntaha) are attributed to motions, distinguishing rectilinear from circular. Rectilinear motion has actual endpoints. Circular motion, being continuous and lack ing intrinsic differentiation, has only hypothetical endpoints unless something external (like alignment or a hypothesized point) provides a distinction. However, there is a discussion: if circular motion is considered as a positional motion (e.g., a body rotating on its axis), it can have actual starts and ends in terms of positions, similar to rectilinear motion, unless the motion is eternal (as in celestial spheres). The note (tanbih) emphasizes that the opposition of ascending and descending motions is based precisely on their intrinsic directions (from and to), not on accidental properties like extreme proximity or distance, which have no connection to motion itself.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that ascending and descending motions are opposed because their endpoints are extremely near or far.
Correction: The tanbih explicitly states that opposition is based on start-ness and end-ness, not on proximity or distance.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the opposition of ascending and descending motions according to the tanbih?
A) The extreme proximity of their endpoints
B) The extreme distance of their endpoints
C) Their start and end being opposed in start-ness and end-ness
D) They are both in the same direction

Key Takeaway
The opposition of motions is based on their intrinsic start and end directions, not on accidental properties like distance.

When you evaluate the 'direction' of your own spiritual journey, do you tend to judge by superficial indicators—how close you feel to God, how near you think you are—or by the intrinsic orientation of your heart's start and end? Which of these is truly a sign of opposition to truth, and how does this lesson reframe your self-assessment?
?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
The Logical Relations of Beginning and End
Defines logical opposition between mabda' and muntaha as contrariety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why mabda' and muntaha are opposites (contraries) when related to each other, but correlatives when related to motion.

Core Idea
Beginning and end are opposites, not correlatives, with each other.

In this passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif, the author clarifies the precise logical relationships between the concepts of 'beginning' (mabda') and 'end' (muntaha). These terms often appear together, but their logical status depends on what they are related to. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly analyzing the opposition of motions.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read the Arabic passage where the author defines the relation of mabda' and muntaha to each other and to motion. Notice the careful distinctions.
Focus on the three types of opposition mentioned: contrariety, privation/possession, and correlation.
2
Identify the logical relations
Identify that when mabda' and muntaha are related to each other, they are contraries. When each is related to motion, they are correlatives.
Why is contrariety chosen over other types? Because both are existent (wujūdiyān).
3
Understand why no correlation
Understand the argument that mabda' and muntaha are not correlatives with each other because one can be conceived without the other.
Correlation requires mutual dependence; here, a beginning can be imagined without an end (e.g., infinite motion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمنتهى أي هذان المفهومان العارضان لا ذاتاهما إذا نسب أحدهما إلى الآخر فتقابلهما تقابل التضاد لا السلب والإيجاب والعدم والملكة لأنهما وجوديان، ولا التضايف لما سنذكره وإذا نسبا إلى ما له المبدأ والمنتهى وهي الحركة كانا متضايفين له فبين كل منهما وبينه أي بين ما له المبدأ والمنتهى تقابل التضايف فإن المبدأ مبدأ لذي المبدأ وذو المبدأ ذو مبدأ للمبدأ وكذا حال المنتهى وذي المنتهى وليس بين المبدأ والمنتهى تضايف فقد يعقل مبدأ لا وبالعكس لجواز أن يفرض حركة لها بداية بلا نهاية أو نهاية بلا بداية، فلا تكافؤ بينهما في التعقل ولا في الوجود فلا تضايف فإن قيل : قد يكون جسم واحد مبدأ لحركة ومنتهى لها أيضاً فكيف يتصور التضاد بينهما مع اجتماعهما في موضوع واحد قلت : هما أعني مفهومي المبدأ والمنتهى غير عارضين للجسم عروضاً أولياً يقال : إنهما يجتمعان فيه بل هما عارضان للأطراف الحاصلة في الأجسام ولايكون طرف واحد مبدأ ومنتهى لحركة واحدة إلا بالفرض وفي زمانين إذ لا يتصور في حركة واحدة مستقيمة أن يكون مبدؤها ومنتهاها طرفاً واحداً، وأما المستديرة فإن مبدأها ومنتهاها نقطة واحدة مفروضة لكنها لا تتصف بهاتين الصفتين في آن واحد فهي وإن كانت واحدة بالذات إلا أنها اثنتان في الاعتبار، وذلك كاف لها في كونها بداية للحركة ونهاية لها، وإنما وسم الفصل بالتنبيه لأن التأمل في مفهومي المبدأ والمنتهى وما نسبا إليه كاف للتصديق بما ذكر فيه فرع على ما مر من أن تضاد الحركات إنما يكون لتضاد المبدأ والمنتهى قالوا : حتى قوله : إذا نسب أحدهما إلى الآخر بالقياس إلى الحركة المستقيمة يشير إليه قوله : فيما أنه لا يتصور في حركة مستقيمة أن يكون مبدؤها ومنتهاها طرفاً واحداً، وقد مر منقولاً الشفاء أنه لم يكن تضاد بين المبدأ والمنتهى لأجل المبدئية والمنتهية إلخ . قوله : وقد يكون جسم واحد بأن يكون مبدأ الحركة ومنتهاها في جسم واحد ،كذا في سييجي في الشفاء. ولا قوله : قلت : هما إلخ خلاصته أن الأضداد لا تجتمع في موضعها القريب والجسم لين قريباً للمبدأ والمنتهى، بل موضوعه الطرف كما أن السواد والبياض يجتمعان في جسم يجتمعان في الموضوع القريب قوله : كانا متضايفين له ظاهر العبارة أن يقول : مضايفين له لأن وضع فاعل لنسبة الفعل إلى الفاعل متعلقاً بغيره مع أن الغير فعل مثل ذلك ووضع تفاعل لنسبته إلى المشتركين فيه من غير قصد إلى تعلق له
And the end: i.e., these two accidental concepts, not their essences, when one is related to the other, their opposition is the opposition of contrariety, not privation and possession or negation and affirmation, because they are existent, nor correlation as we shall mention. And when they are related to that which has the beginning and end, namely motion, then each is a correlative of it, so between each of them and it (i.e., that which has the beginning and end) is the opposition of correlation. For the beginning is a beginning of that which has a beginning, and that which has a beginning has a beginning for the beginning, and likewise for the end and that which has an end. And there is no correlation between the beginning and the end, for a beginning can be conceived without an end and vice versa, because it is possible to assume a motion with a beginning without an end or an end without a beginning, so there is no mutual dependence between them in conception or existence, hence no correlation. If it is said: a single body can be a beginning of a motion and also an end of it, so how can there be opposition between them when they coexist in one subject? I reply: they, i.e., the concepts of beginning and end, do not inhere in the body primarily (it is said they coexist in it), but rather they inhere in the extremities that occur in bodies. And a single extremity cannot be beginning and end of one motion except by assumption and in two times, for it is inconceivable in a single rectilinear motion that its beginning and end be one extremity. As for circular motion, its beginning and end are a single assumed point, but it does not possess these two attributes simultaneously; so although it is one in essence, it is two in consideration, and that suffices for it to be a beginning and an end of the motion. And the section was marked as a note because reflection on the two concepts of beginning and end and what they are related to is sufficient for believing what is mentioned therein. A branch on the basis that the opposition of motions is only due to the opposition of beginning and end. They said: until his statement: 'when one is related to the other with respect to rectilinear motion' refers to his statement: 'it is inconceivable in rectilinear motion that its beginning and end be one extremity', and it has been transmitted from al-Shifa' that there was no opposition between beginning and end on account of beginningness and endness etc. His statement: 'And a single body can be such that it is the beginning of a motion and its end in a single body', as in—it will come in al-Shifa'. And his statement: 'I reply: they etc.' The summary is that opposites do not coexist in their proximate subject, and the body is not the proximate subject for beginning and end, but rather the extremity is their subject, just as black and white coexist in a body but coexist in the proximate subject. His statement: 'they are correlatives of it'—the apparent wording would be to say: 'correlative to it' because the form fā'il indicates the attribution of an action to the agent relating to something else while that other does a similar action, and the form tafā'ul indicates the attribution to the participants in it without intending relation to it.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage defines the logical relations between the concepts of beginning (mabda') and end (muntaha) and motion. It first states that when one relates 'beginning' and 'end' to each other, they are opposites (mutadāddān) because they are both existent concepts (wujūdiyān), not like privation and possession. When each is related to motion (which has a beginning and an end), they are correlatives (mutadāyifān). However, beginning and end are not correlatives with each other because one can conceive a beginning without an end or vice versa, which shows no mutual dependence. The passage then addresses an objection: how can beginning and end be opposites if they coexist in a single body (e.g., a body that is both start and end of motion)? The answer is that the concepts of beginning and end do not inhere in the body itself but in the extremities (aṭrāf) that occur in bodies. In rectilinear motion, a single extremity cannot be both beginning and end simultaneously; in circular motion, the assumed point is one in essence but two in consideration (different aspects), so it does not have both attributes at the same time. The passage then notes that the section is called a 'note' because reflection suffices. It continues with a 'branch' (far') reiterating that opposition of motions is due to opposition of beginning and end, and includes references to al-Shifa' and a grammatical note on the word 'mutadāyifīn' (correlatives), explaining that the form tafā'ul is more appropriate for mutual relation without one-sided dependency.

Key Terms
مبدأ
منتهى
تضاد
تضايف
وجوديان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mabda' and muntaha are correlatives because they always come together in motion.
Correction: They are not correlatives because one can be conceived without the other; correlation requires mutual dependence.

Checkpoint
Why are mabda' and muntaha not correlatives (mutadāyifān) with each other?
A) Because they are both existent.
B) Because they are opposites.
C) Because one can be conceived without the other, showing no mutual dependence.
D) Because they inhere in the same body.

Key Takeaway
Mabda' and muntaha are contraries when compared directly, but each is a correlative of motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a good deed you started with sincere intention but later abandoned because you feared you could not complete it perfectly. How does the lesson's teaching that a beginning can exist without an end free you from that fear? Will you restart that deed today, trusting that your beginning is real even if the end is not yet realized?
?
Consider a sin you have been struggling to leave. You may feel that since you began it, you are trapped in a chain that must run its course. But the passage says the beginning and end are not correlatives—they are not bound to each other. Can you cut the sin off right now, at this moment, without waiting for a 'proper' end? What is holding you back?
?
The passage calls beginning and end 'existent' (وجوديان). Reflect on the beginnings in your life that you have dismissed as insignificant or unreal because they were small. If they are truly existent in the sight of Allah, how should you value them? What beginning will you honor today by nurturing it instead of ignoring it?

Resolving the Coexistence of Beginning and End in a Single Body
Answers objection on coexistence of mabda' and muntaha in one body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how mabda' and muntaha can coexist in a single body without contradicting their opposition, especially in rectilinear versus circular motion.

Core Idea
A single extremity can be both beginning and end only in assumption or in different times/aspects.

An objection arises: if beginning and end are opposites, how can they both be present in one body? The author addresses this by distinguishing between the subject of these concepts (the extremity, not the body itself) and by analyzing rectilinear and circular motion. This lesson explores that resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage presenting the objection and the author's reply. Pay attention to the logical flow.
The objection claims that a single body can be both start and end of a motion, which would imply coexistence of opposites.
2
Identify the proximate subject
Notice that the author says the concepts do not inhere in the body primarily but in the extremities (aṭrāf) occurring in bodies.
This distinction resolves the apparent contradiction: the body is not the proximate subject.
3
Compare rectilinear and circular motion
Understand that in rectilinear motion, beginning and end are distinct points; in circular motion, the same point is considered beginning and end in different aspects or times.
This preserves opposition because the same point does not have both attributes simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمنتهى أي هذان المفهومان العارضان لا ذاتاهما إذا نسب أحدهما إلى الآخر فتقابلهما تقابل التضاد لا السلب والإيجاب والعدم والملكة لأنهما وجوديان، ولا التضايف لما سنذكره وإذا نسبا إلى ما له المبدأ والمنتهى وهي الحركة كانا متضايفين له فبين كل منهما وبينه أي بين ما له المبدأ والمنتهى تقابل التضايف فإن المبدأ مبدأ لذي المبدأ وذو المبدأ ذو مبدأ للمبدأ وكذا حال المنتهى وذي المنتهى وليس بين المبدأ والمنتهى تضايف فقد يعقل مبدأ لا وبالعكس لجواز أن يفرض حركة لها بداية بلا نهاية أو نهاية بلا بداية، فلا تكافؤ بينهما في التعقل ولا في الوجود فلا تضايف فإن قيل : قد يكون جسم واحد مبدأ لحركة ومنتهى لها أيضاً فكيف يتصور التضاد بينهما مع اجتماعهما في موضوع واحد قلت : هما أعني مفهومي المبدأ والمنتهى غير عارضين للجسم عروضاً أولياً يقال : إنهما يجتمعان فيه بل هما عارضان للأطراف الحاصلة في الأجسام ولايكون طرف واحد مبدأ ومنتهى لحركة واحدة إلا بالفرض وفي زمانين إذ لا يتصور في حركة واحدة مستقيمة أن يكون مبدؤها ومنتهاها طرفاً واحداً، وأما المستديرة فإن مبدأها ومنتهاها نقطة واحدة مفروضة لكنها لا تتصف بهاتين الصفتين في آن واحد فهي وإن كانت واحدة بالذات إلا أنها اثنتان في الاعتبار، وذلك كاف لها في كونها بداية للحركة ونهاية لها، وإنما وسم الفصل بالتنبيه لأن التأمل في مفهومي المبدأ والمنتهى وما نسبا إليه كاف للتصديق بما ذكر فيه فرع على ما مر من أن تضاد الحركات إنما يكون لتضاد المبدأ والمنتهى قالوا : حتى قوله : إذا نسب أحدهما إلى الآخر بالقياس إلى الحركة المستقيمة يشير إليه قوله : فيما أنه لا يتصور في حركة مستقيمة أن يكون مبدؤها ومنتهاها طرفاً واحداً، وقد مر منقولاً الشفاء أنه لم يكن تضاد بين المبدأ والمنتهى لأجل المبدئية والمنتهية إلخ . قوله : وقد يكون جسم واحد بأن يكون مبدأ الحركة ومنتهاها في جسم واحد ،كذا في سييجي في الشفاء. ولا قوله : قلت : هما إلخ خلاصته أن الأضداد لا تجتمع في موضعها القريب والجسم لين قريباً للمبدأ والمنتهى، بل موضوعه الطرف كما أن السواد والبياض يجتمعان في جسم يجتمعان في الموضوع القريب قوله : كانا متضايفين له ظاهر العبارة أن يقول : مضايفين له لأن وضع فاعل لنسبة الفعل إلى الفاعل متعلقاً بغيره مع أن الغير فعل مثل ذلك ووضع تفاعل لنسبته إلى المشتركين فيه من غير قصد إلى تعلق له
And the end: i.e., these two accidental concepts, not their essences, when one is related to the other, their opposition is the opposition of contrariety, not privation and possession or negation and affirmation, because they are existent, nor correlation as we shall mention. And when they are related to that which has the beginning and end, namely motion, then each is a correlative of it, so between each of them and it (i.e., that which has the beginning and end) is the opposition of correlation. For the beginning is a beginning of that which has a beginning, and that which has a beginning has a beginning for the beginning, and likewise for the end and that which has an end. And there is no correlation between the beginning and the end, for a beginning can be conceived without an end and vice versa, because it is possible to assume a motion with a beginning without an end or an end without a beginning, so there is no mutual dependence between them in conception or existence, hence no correlation. Commentary
This passage defines the logical relations between the concepts of beginning (mabda') and end (muntaha) and motion. Misconception & Correction
